The ProLibertad Youth/Student Network, The Puerto Rican Nationalist Youth,
The Center for Puerto Rican Studies and SLAM are announcing our joint
educational: �Building the Puerto Rican Movement: PAST, PRESENT AND FUTURE�.

The Puerto Rican Independence movement has always been alive in New York
City!!  It has been young people and young adults that have carried on the
struggle for freedom and revolution!!  Come and join us for a night of
Revolutionary Entertainment and Education.  Learn about the organizations
that were educating, organizing and mobilizing Boricuas in the Seventies!!

Come and learn about your REVOLUTIONARY ROOTS!!  COME AND LEARN ABOUT THE
PAST AND HELP BUILD THE PRESENT AND FUTURE!! WE HAVE  A NEW PANELIST ON
THE PANEL!!

Join us for a Special Presentation by Powerful and inspirational Nuyorican
Poet Rafael Landron!!  "Rafi's Newyorican Anti-war Expressions" is an
attempt to inspire others to nurture the growing anti-imperialist movement
using creativity and greatness. The pieces are meant to spur action! For me,
after the performance is as important if not more so than the pieces
themselves because I will encourage folks to get together and organize their
own expressions of resistance for the future.

Friday March 26th, 2004 at 6:30pm at
Hunter College West Building Second Floor Room 217
(e68th St. and Lexington Avenue)
Take the 6 Train to e68th St. and Lexington Avenue

For more information call 718-601-4751 or email ProLibertad@...
http://ProLibertadWeb.Tripod.com

PANEL PRESENTATIONS BY:

Frank Velgara, El Comite-MINP
EL Comite-MINP was a Political organization that emerged from the democratic
rights struggles around housing, and education and Health in NYC.  El
Comite-MINP supported the National Liberation struggle of Puerto Rico
through Working Class Struggle.

Carlos Rovira, The Young Lords Party
The Young Lords were a powerful Puerto Rican Revolutionary organization that
fought for the human and civil rights for all Working Class People of Color.
They were dedicated to the freedom of Puerto Rico and the fight for
socialism.

Alice Hernandez, The PR Nationalist Party
The Puerto Rican Nationalist Party, was the Party of Don Pedro Albizu
Campos.  The Party has continued the struggle for Puerto Rican independence
for decades both in PR and New York City.

Blanca Vasquez, Latin Women�s Collective
The Latin Women's Collective was based in New York City, their political
efforts on behalf of women's issues created an amazing legacy of Latina
feminism and empowerment.

Eli Roman, The Puerto Rican Student Union
The PRSU was an organization of Puerto Rican Youth based in colleges in New
York that organized for freedom, civil rights and unity among poor working
class youth and people of color.

Jose Velasquez, The Puerto Rican Socialist Party
The PSP was one of the largest Socialist organizations in the Puerto Rican 
community; they demanded the Independence of Puerto Rico, the democratic 
human rights of people, and for socialism in Puerto Rico.

Sender:"ProLibertad Campaign" <prolibertad@...>
Post Date/Time:2004-03-04 11:13:49
Subject:Building the Puerto Rican Movement
Message:

The ProLibertad Youth/Student Network, The Puerto Rican Nationalist Youth,
The Center for Puerto Rican Studies and SLAM are announcing our joint
educational: �Building the Puerto Rican Movement: PAST, PRESENT AND FUTURE�.

The Puerto Rican Independence movement has always been alive in New York
City!!  It has been young people and young adults that have carried on the
struggle for freedom and revolution!!  Come and join us for a night of
Revolutionary Entertainment and Education.  Learn about the organizations
that were educating, organizing and mobilizing Boricuas in the Seventies!!

Come and learn about your REVOLUTIONARY ROOTS!!  COME AND LEARN ABOUT THE
PAST AND HELP BUILD THE PRESENT AND FUTURE!! WE HAVE  A NEW PANELIST ON
THE PANEL!!

Join us for a Special Presentation by Powerful and inspirational Nuyorican
Poet Rafael Landron!!  "Rafi's Newyorican Anti-war Expressions" is an
attempt to inspire others to nurture the growing anti-imperialist movement
using creativity and greatness. The pieces are meant to spur action! For me,
after the performance is as important if not more so than the pieces
themselves because I will encourage folks to get together and organize their
own expressions of resistance for the future.

Friday March 26th, 2004 at 6:30pm at
Hunter College West Building Second Floor Room 217
(e68th St. and Lexington Avenue)
Take the 6 Train to e68th St. and Lexington Avenue

For more information call 718-601-4751 or email ProLibertad@...
http://ProLibertadWeb.Tripod.com

PANEL PRESENTATIONS BY:

Frank Velgara, El Comite-MINP
EL Comite-MINP was a Political organization that emerged from the democratic
rights struggles around housing, and education and Health in NYC.  El
Comite-MINP supported the National Liberation struggle of Puerto Rico
through Working Class Struggle.

Carlos Rovira, The Young Lords Party
The Young Lords were a powerful Puerto Rican Revolutionary organization that
fought for the human and civil rights for all Working Class People of Color.
They were dedicated to the freedom of Puerto Rico and the fight for
socialism.

Alice Hernandez, The PR Nationalist Party
The Puerto Rican Nationalist Party, was the Party of Don Pedro Albizu
Campos.  The Party has continued the struggle for Puerto Rican independence
for decades both in PR and New York City.

Blanca Vasquez, Latin Women�s Collective
The Latin Women's Collective was based in New York City, their political
efforts on behalf of women's issues created an amazing legacy of Latina
feminism and empowerment.

Eli Roman, The Puerto Rican Student Union
The PRSU was an organization of Puerto Rican Youth based in colleges in New
York that organized for freedom, civil rights and unity among poor working
class youth and people of color.

Jose Velasquez, The Puerto Rican Socialist Party
The PSP was one of the largest Socialist organizations in the Puerto Rican
community; they demanded the Independence of Puerto Rico, the democratic
human rights of people, and for socialism in Puerto Rico.

_________________________________________________________________

Post Date/Time:2004-03-16 19:04:44
Subject:Rafael Cancel Miranda
Message:

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign has two major announcements:

1.  La Musica De Rafael Cancel Miranda is a CD of Don Rafael Cancel 
Miranda�s poetry put to music with the vocal stylings of Mmadu Onyeuwa and 
Jenny Santiago!!

This 15 track CD is an amazing compilation of the poetry of former Puerto 
Rican Political Prisoner Rafael Cancel Miranda set to tropical, jazz and 
many other musical styles.

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign is selling this CD for $20 a copy.  The 
proceeds of this CD go to the publishing of Rafael Cancel Miranda�s newest 
poetry anthology, as well as the campaign to free the Puerto Rican Political 
Prisoners!!

To order a copy of La Musica de Rafael Cancel Miranda please contact 
ProLibertad at 718-601-4751 or email us at ProLibertad@...

2.  The ProLibertad FReedom Campaign's website has been updated for March 
15th: http://ProLibertadWeb.Tripod.com

_______________________________________________________________________________

after the performance is as important if not more so than the pieces
themselves because I will encourage folks to get together and organize their
own expressions of resistance for the future.

Friday March 26th, 2004 at 6:30pm at
Hunter College West Building Second Floor Room 217
(e68th St. and Lexington Avenue)
Take the 6 Train to e68th St. and Lexington Avenue

For more information call 718-601-4751 or email ProLibertad@...
http://ProLibertadWeb.Tripod.com

PANEL PRESENTATIONS BY:

Frank Velgara, El Comite-MINP
EL Comite-MINP was a Political organization that emerged from the democratic
rights struggles around housing, and education and Health in NYC. El
Comite-MINP supported the National Liberation struggle of Puerto Rico
through Working Class Struggle.

Carlos Rovira, The Young Lords Party
The Young Lords were a powerful Puerto Rican Revolutionary organization that
fought for the human and civil rights for all Working Class People of Color.
They were dedicated to the freedom of Puerto Rico and the fight for
socialism.

Alice Hernandez, The PR Nationalist Party
The Puerto Rican Nationalist Party, was the Party of Don Pedro Albizu
Campos. The Party has continued the struggle for Puerto Rican independence
for decades both in PR and New York City.

Blanca Vasquez, Latin Women�s Collective
The Latin Women's Collective was based in New York City, their political
efforts on behalf of women's issues created an amazing legacy of Latina
feminism and empowerment.

Eli Roman, The Puerto Rican Student Union
The PRSU was an organization of Puerto Rican Youth based in colleges in New
York that organized for freedom, civil rights and unity among poor working
class youth and people of color.

Jose Velasquez, The Puerto Rican Socialist Party
The PSP was one of the largest Socialist organizations in the Puerto Rican
community; they demanded the Independence of Puerto Rico, the democratic
human rights of people, and for socialism in Puerto Rico.

Post ID:3404
Sender:"ProLibertad Campaign" <prolibertad@...>
Post Date/Time:2004-03-28 20:10:01
Subject:Richie Perez Remembered
Message:

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign is deeply saddened to announce the passing 
our ally, mentor, friend, warrior, teacher and companero de lucha: Richie 
Perez.

Richie Perez was a powerful force for social change and touched the hearts 
and minds of everyone he worked with throughout the decades.  As many know, 
Richie was a leader in the Young Lords, then in The Puerto Rican 
Revolutionary Workers Organization, was a founder of the National Congress 
for Puerto Rican Rights/Justice Committee, a media activist for 
Latino/Puerto Rican positive representation, a committed Revolutionary, and 
a long-time Internationalist.

Richie inspired and motivated people to work for justice on all levels; his 
infectious commitment to justice and social change inspired several 
generations of youth to continue the fight against Police Brutality and 
racist violence, to free Puerto Rican Political Prisoners, to liberate 
Puerto Rico, to create positive spaces for Latin@s in the media and to unite 
into powerful political coalitions of people of color.  Richie believed in 
serving the people and lived his life in the pursuit of revolutionary change 
and the formation of better world for all people.

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign believes that this is Richie�s greatest 
legacy: Richie trained, taught and inspired many young leaders.  Richie 
believed in youth governance and creating supportive spaces for young people 
in social justice work.  He taught with compassion and support; he trained 
with insightful political analysis and instilled the importance of critical 
political analysis in all that we do.  He impressed upon us the need to work 
collectively, to plan effectively, and to build with our allies.

Richie�s passing has been felt by many communities and will be mourned for a 
long time.  Richie was a lot more than just a Puerto Rican leader; he was a 
working class leader, a people of color leader, he was an inspiration to all 
people.  He truly embraced all oppressed peoples, as his brothers and 
sisters.  He, much like Che, felt that any injustice committed against any 
person was an injustice to him.  He embodied the most powerful and essential 
qualities of the revolutionary; he was motivated by great love and the need 
to see people be free.

Richie asked us to remember his last request at his vigil, �It is time to up 
the ante�.  We must carry on our work and �up the ante� in all we do. This 
is our call to action, this is how we remember this amazing man, by �uping 
the ante� in our work.  We must finally learn from and act upon Richie�s 
lessons: we have to move away from our sectarianism, we must come together 
and be accountable to our communities, and we must smash the state together. 
  It is time to scream like they did in Lares, Puerto Rico!!

On a personal note, I, Benjamin Ramos, can still remember the first time I 
met Richie Perez, it was March 29th, 1995; a meeting at CSS for Racial 
Justice Day.  I was there researching Racial Justioce Day and the police 
brutality movement for Urban Latino Magazine.  I sat down with this 
incredible man who had returned my calls and invited me to one of the 
planning meetings for Racial Justice Day.  He took out time to sit down with 
this teenage �wanna-be freelance� journalist, who was in way over his head, 
and broke down the issues piece by piece, all the while inspiring me and 
making me hunger for justice.  I stayed on with the Justice Committee, after 
my article was written, because Richie had sparked in me this need to make 
change.  He set me on the path that I now follow with ProLibertad, the 
Vieques Support Campaign, and El Frente Socialista de Puerto Rico.  He 
trained me, taught me, motivated me, and most importantly supported me along 
the way.

I love you Richie, my father, mentor and friend.  We will up the ante, in 
your honor and for the betterment of our people.

FOR RICHIE,
FOR PUERTO RICO,
FOR JUSTICE AND PEACE!!

The public viewing will be:
Monday and Tuesday, March 30th at
Frank Campbell Funeral Home
1076 Madison Ave (81st.)
The hours are:
Monday 4-5pm & 7-9
Tuesday 2-5pm & 7-9

LATIN@S POR MUMIA

JOIN THE LATIN@S FOR MUMIA CONTINGENT!!

Latin@s for Mumia Next general NYC Meeting
Tuesday April 6th, 2004 at 6:30pm
St. Mary's Church
521 W126th St. between Broadwy and Amsterdam Avenue
(take the 1 or 9 trian to W125th St.)

�Information on the mobilization
�Latin@s for Mumia Contingent
�Information on tickets and buses
�Materials in Spanish
�Next Meeting

544-1577 or (212) 749-8024 and email us at: LatinsforMumia@...

The Socialist Front of Puerto Rico vigorously condemns the assassination of 
Palestinian leader Ahmad Yassin that was recently carried out at the orders 
of Israeli State headed by the war criminal Ariel Sharon.  There is no doubt 
that Sharon attempts to escalate the conflict in Palestine with the 
objective of advancing his most beloved project:  to expel the Palestinian 
People from the occupied territories.


No one in the world that aspires to have peace can feel safe while the 
reigns of any government are in the hands of someone like Sharon who 
embodies the slide toward barbarism that is characteristic of the �new world 
order�.  The main guardian of that order is, of course, the U.S. military 
machine that today occupies Iraq and that intervenes directly in scores of 
countries. But this is precisely its weakness: throughout the planet 
imperialism is faced with a new and growing resistance.  It is also for this 
reason the admiration and solidarity grows with the people of Palestine who 
are always on the front lines of the resistance to imperialist and colonial 
brutality.

Similarly, we also condemn the hypocrisy of the U.S. government who on the 
one hand criticizes the assassination of Ahmad Yassin and on the other 
continues arming his assassins and blocking all attempts at the United 
Nations and other international forums to condemn Israel for its crimes.  We 
know that the Palestinian People will recover from this blow and that they 
will continue strengthening their resistance and to serve as an example to 
all the worlds peoples.

Long Live a Free and Sovereign Palestine!

Rafael Bernabe, Spokesperson
Socialist Front of Puerto Rico
March 30, 2004

LATIN@S FOR MUMIA ABU-JAMAL
MOBILIZE TO APRIL 24, 2004!!
Free Mumia and All Political Prisoners!
!ALL OUT TO PHILADELPHIA!

MASS DEMONSTRATION TO FREE MUMIA ABU-JAMAL!

JOIN THE LATIN@S FOR MUMIA CONTINGENT!!
There will be a mass demonstration in Philadelphia and in San Francisco on 
April 24, 2004.  Mumia will be 50 years old on that day, having spent almost 
half of his life in prison for a crime that the evidence proves he did NOT 
committ. On April 24th, Mumia�s new book, We Want Freedom, a living history 
of the Black Panther Party, will be published!  We will also join Mumia�s 
friends, family and comrades from the Black Panther Party for the biggest 
book signing party in history will be held in Philadelphia as we celebrate 
Mumia�s birthday in the streets, marching to demand his immediate release.

Buses will leave from New York City for Philadelphia in order to insure that 
the solidarity and support for our brother Mumia by Latinas and Latinos is 
felt in Philadelphia.

Prolibertad, The Vieques Support Campaign, The N.Y. Committee of the 
Nationalist Party of Puerto Rico, La Iglesia San Romero De Las Americas, The 
ProLibertad Youth Student  Network,  The Nationalist Youth, Socialist Front 
of Puerto Rico (New York), and Casa De Las Americas are making this call to 
involve as many other Latin@ organizations and individuals as possible.  Be 
part of this effort!

For More Information About Latin@s For Mumia:
(718) 601-4751 (212) 749-8024 or
email: Latinsformumia@...
Buses Leave From 33rd Street and 8th Avenue, Manhattan
(In Front Of The Main Post Office)
BUSES WILL LEAVE AT 8:00 A.M.�SHARP!!

Subject:Latin@s for Mumia
Message:

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign has updated our website for April, please 
check ou the Latin@s for Mumia page:  http://ProLibertadWeb.Tripod.com

______________________________________________________________________________

LATIN@S FOR MUMIA ABU-JAMAL
MOBILIZE TO APRIL 24, 2004!!
Free Mumia and All Political Prisoners!
!ALL OUT TO PHILADELPHIA!

MASS DEMONSTRATION TO FREE MUMIA ABU-JAMAL!

JOIN THE LATIN@S FOR MUMIA CONTINGENT!!
There will be a mass demonstration in Philadelphia and in San Francisco on
April 24, 2004.  Mumia will be 50 years old on that day, having spent almost
half of his life in prison for a crime that the evidence proves he did NOT
committ. On April 24th, Mumia�s new book, We Want Freedom, a living history
of the Black Panther Party, will be published!  We will also join Mumia�s
friends, family and comrades from the Black Panther Party for the biggest
book signing party in history will be held in Philadelphia as we celebrate
Mumia�s birthday in the streets, marching to demand his immediate release.

Buses will leave from New York City for Philadelphia in order to insure that
the solidarity and support for our brother Mumia by Latinas and Latinos is
felt in Philadelphia.

Prolibertad, The Vieques Support Campaign, The N.Y. Committee of the
Nationalist Party of Puerto Rico, La Iglesia San Romero De Las Americas, The
ProLibertad Youth Student  Network,  The Nationalist Youth, Socialist Front
of Puerto Rico (New York), and Casa De Las Americas are making this call to
involve as many other Latin@ organizations and individuals as possible.  Be
part of this effort!

For More Information About Latin@s For Mumia:
(718) 601-4751 (212) 749-8024
Buses Leave From 33rd Street and 8th Avenue, Manhattan
(In Front Of The Main Post Office)
BUSES WILL LEAVE AT 8:00 A.M.�SHARP!!

Post ID:3414
Sender:"ProLibertad Campaign" <prolibertad@...>
Post Date/Time:2004-04-19 09:32:58
Subject:May 1st Anti-Military Demo.
Message:

MAY 1ST PICKET AND RALLY

On May 1st join the Pro-libertad Student Youth Network, La Juventud
Nacionalista, Justice for Youth, and S.L.A.M at a Rally and Picket in front 
of the U.S. Military Recruitment Center in Fordham Rd. and Grand concourse.


- Fight against the U.S. occupation in Iraq and the world!!!!
- End the military occupancy in Puerto Rico!!!!
- End ROTC recruitment in schools!!!!
- Get the NYPD out of our schools!!!!
- Stop the recruitment of our brothers and sisters!!!!


Guests Speakers and Poetry

JOIN US AT NOON!!!!!!!!
Fordham Rd and Grand Concourse in front of the recruitment center

Bring your flags, noise makers, and signs and help us fight recruitment in
our neighborhoods!!!!


Pro-libertad Student Youth Network is here to create a coalition of 
individuals and organizations to commit to educating and mobilizing for the 
support of the Puerto Rican Political Prisoners, the Puerto Rican national 
Liberation struggle, and all other social justice movements.  As always, in 
unity there is strength, strength allows us to struggle, and struggle leads 
to liberation.

Juventud Nacionalista Puertorrique�a (JNP) /The Puerto Rican Nationalist
Youth (PRNY) is the youth wing of the Puerto Rican Nationalist Party (PNPR).
Our organization is founded upon Nationalism, Patriotism, Valor, Sacrifice,
Love, and Duty to our Nation, Puerto Rico. The PRNY seeks to bring together
and educate young Puerto Ricans on their history, national identity,
culture, community, and the struggle for Puerto Rican independence against
U.S. colonial rule.


If any organizations are interested in endorsing please email 
Pequena26@...

recruitment. This tape takes a critical look at the military�'92s promises

by veterans who have actually been there. Speaker: Benjamun: Ramos from 
Prolibertad Rayblin Vargas from Justice 4 Youth

Vieques: Transforming Dreams to Reality: The Struggle Continues!
Vieques Conference 2004
May 15-18 Washington, DC
An Invitational Conference

Convening Organizations:
Judith Conde, Vieques Women's Alliance
Armando Torres/Robert Rabin, Committee for the Rescue and Development of 
Vieques
Josie Pantojas/Che Paraliticci/Pilar Bel�ndez, Todo Puerto Rico con Vieques
Wanda Col�n Cortez, Caribbean Project for Justice and Peace Conference 
Planning Committee
Natalia Cardona/Denise Davis Darryl Jordan, American Friends Service 
Committee
Sonia Ivette Due�o John Lindsay-Poland, Fellowship of Reconciliation
Tara Thornton, Military Toxics Project
Marisol Morales/Alejandro Molina, National BoricuaHuman Rights Network
Esperanza Martell/Frank Velgara, ProLibertad Freedom Campaign
Dr. Carlos Correa, United Church of Christ
Eliezer Valentin-Casta�on United Methodist Church,General Board of Church 
and Society
Carlos Rovira, Vieques Support Campaign
David Cline, Chairperson Veterans for Peace

Please join us Saturday May 15 - Tuesday May18 at Gonzaga College High 
School
900 North Capitol NW

Washington, D.C. (near Union Station Metro)

Last May 1, the U.S. Navy transferred Vieques lands under its use to the US 
Department of the Interior's Fish and Wildlife Service, ending over sixty 
years of bombing and target practice on the populated island. The Vieques 
community, through civil disobedience and with support from organizations 
and religious denominations from all sectors of civil society both 
nationally and internationally, was finally able to rid itself of decades of 
pounding by live ammunition.
Please join us for a weekend of activity as we assess and develop strategies 
for future work for Vieques. The strategies developed will allow 
participants to go back to their organizations and communities for 
follow-up.

This conference is by invitation to plan strategies for the Vieques 
struggle. Planning sessions will take place on Saturday and Sunday during 
the day. Sunday, May 16th in the evening there will be a public presentation 
by Vieques groups.

For those who participate on Monday, May 17, there will be meetings with 
elected officials and national organizations to pursue action and support 
for the strategies being developed.

Schedule:

Saturday, May 15: 9:00 a.m. - 9:00 p.m. Strategy sessions

Sunday, May 16: 9:30 a.m. - 2:00 p.m. Strategy sessions
2:00 - 5:00 p.m. Preparation for Mon/Tues meetings
7:00 - 9:30 p.m. Public event

Mon. May 17-Tues. May 18 Meetings with federal officials & national groups

For more information, contact Sonia Ivette Due�o, coordinating on behalf of 
the Planning Committee at 202-488-5613, Fax: 202-488-5639 or by email at 
SDueno@.... Information on housing and transportation in Washington 
will be sent with confirmation of registration.

Military Myths: focuses on the racial / economic profiling politics behind
recruitment. This tape takes a critical look at the military�'92s promises
of travel, money for education and job training. It considers how media
representations of war and military life compare to the reality of war told
by veterans who have actually been there. Speaker: Benjamun: Ramos from
Prolibertad Rayblin Vargas from Justice 4 Youth

Thursday, April 29th, 2004
6:30pm Donations

700 Elton Ave. 2nd Floor The Bronx, NYC 2 0r 5 train to 149th St. & 3rd Ave.

MAY 1ST PICKET AND RALLY

On May 1st at 12pm in the Bronx join the Pro-libertad Student Youth Network,
La Juventud Nacionalista, Justice for Youth, S.L.A.M, The International 
Socialist
Organization, and SNAFU at a Rally and Picket in front of the U.S. Military 
Recruitment
Center in Fordham Rd. and Grand concourse.


- Fight against the U.S. occupation in Iraq and the world!!!!
- End the military occupancy in Puerto Rico!!!!
- End ROTC recruitment in schools!!!!
- Get the NYPD out of our schools!!!!
- Stop the recruitment of our brothers and sisters!!!!


Guests Speakers and Poetry

JOIN US AT 12 NOON!!!!!!!!
Fordham Rd and Grand Concourse in front of the recruitment center.
Take the D train to Fordham Rd.

Bring your flags, noise makers, and signs and help us fight recruitment
inour neighborhoods!!!!

Pro-libertad Student Youth Network is here to create a coalition of
individuals and organizations to commit to educating and mobilizing for
the support of the Puerto Rican Political Prisoners, the Puerto Rican
national Liberation struggle, and all other social justice movements.
As always, in unity there is strength, strength allows us to struggle,
and struggle leads to liberation.

Juventud Nacionalista Puertorrique�a (JNP) /The Puerto Rican Nationalist
Youth (PRNY) is the youth wing of the Puerto Rican Nationalist Party
(PNPR). Our organization is founded upon Nationalism, Patriotism, Valor,
Sacrifice,Love, and Duty to our Nation, Puerto Rico. The PRNY seeks to bring
together and educate young Puerto Ricans on their history, national 
identity,
culture, community, and the struggle for Puerto Rican independence against
U.S. colonial rule.

Pequena26@...

La Juventud Nacionalista
Justice for Peace
S.L.A.M.
International Socialist Organization
S.N.A.F.U.

Vieques: Transforming Dreams to Reality: The Struggle Continues!
Vieques Conference 2004
May 15-18 Washington, DC
An Invitational Conference

Convening Organizations:
Judith Conde, Vieques Women's Alliance
Armando Torres/Robert Rabin, Committee for the Rescue and Development of 
Vieques
Josie Pantojas/Che Paraliticci/Pilar Bel�ndez, Todo Puerto Rico con Vieques
Wanda Col�n Cortez, Caribbean Project for Justice and Peace Conference 
Planning Committee
Natalia Cardona/Denise Davis Darryl Jordan, American Friends Service 
Committee
Sonia Ivette Due�o John Lindsay-Poland, Fellowship of Reconciliation
Tara Thornton, Military Toxics Project
Marisol Morales/Alejandro Molina, National BoricuaHuman Rights Network
Esperanza Martell/Frank Velgara, ProLibertad Freedom Campaign
Dr. Carlos Correa, United Church of Christ
Eliezer Valentin-Casta�on United Methodist Church,General Board of Church 
and Society
Carlos Rovira, Vieques Support Campaign
David Cline, Chairperson Veterans for Peace

Please join us Saturday May 15 - Tuesday May18 at Gonzaga College High 
School
900 North Capitol NW

Washington, D.C. (near Union Station Metro)

Last May 1, the U.S. Navy transferred Vieques lands under its use to the US 
Department of the Interior's Fish and Wildlife Service, ending over sixty 
years of bombing and target practice on the populated island. The Vieques 
community, through civil disobedience and with support from organizations 
and religious denominations from all sectors of civil society both 
nationally and internationally, was finally able to rid itself of decades of 
pounding by live ammunition.
Please join us for a weekend of activity as we assess and develop strategies 
for future work for Vieques. The strategies developed will allow 
participants to go back to their organizations and communities for 
follow-up.

This conference is by invitation to plan strategies for the Vieques 
struggle. Planning sessions will take place on Saturday and Sunday during 
the day. Sunday, May 16th in the evening there will be a public presentation 
by Vieques groups.

For those who participate on Monday, May 17, there will be meetings with 
elected officials and national organizations to pursue action and support 
for the strategies being developed.

Schedule:

Saturday, May 15: 9:00 a.m. - 9:00 p.m. Strategy sessions

Sunday, May 16: 9:30 a.m. - 2:00 p.m. Strategy sessions
2:00 - 5:00 p.m. Preparation for Mon/Tues meetings
7:00 - 9:30 p.m. Public event

Mon. May 17-Tues. May 18 Meetings with federal officials & national groups

For more information, contact Sonia Ivette Due�o, coordinating on behalf of 
the Planning Committee at 202-488-5613, Fax: 202-488-5639 or by email at 
SDueno@.... Information on housing and transportation in Washington 
will be sent with confirmation of registration.

Post ID:3427
Sender:"ProLibertad Campaign" <prolibertad@...>
Post Date/Time:2004-05-18 09:33:41
Subject:ProLibertad 10th Anniversary
Message:

Join the ProLibertad Freedom Campaign for our annual Reception for the 
Puerto Rico Delegation of the United Nations De-Colonization Committee 
Hearing!!

Every year a Delegation from Puerto Rico comes to the United Nations to 
testify to the U.N. De-Colonization Committee, to make the case for the 
liberation of Puerto Rico and the release of the Puerto Rican Political 
Prisoners and Prisoners of War.

This delegation is made of various activists from the different 
organizations that fight for the independence of Puerto Rico.  The 
ProLibertad Freedom Campaign organizes a reception for this delegation as an 
opportunity for allies of the Puerto Rican independence movement to converse 
with the delegation about Puerto Rico in the United Nations and to hear an 
update about the various struggles in Puerto Rico.

*The workers Struggle in Puerto Rico!!
*Vieques and the Four Ds!!
*The Puerto Rican Political Prisoners!!
*Puerto Rico and the International Struggle!!
*U.S. Imperialism and Colonialism!!

Monday June 14th, 2004 at 6:30pm
Hunter College West Building Second Floor Room 217
(Take the 6 train to E68th St. and Lexington Avenue)
Food, Literature, and Conversation!!
Donation: $10 (No one will be turned away)


******************************************************************************* 
                                                 VERY IMPORTANT SAVE THE 
DATE!!
*******************************************************************************

Dear Allies, Friends, Comrades:

The 10th Anniversary Celebration of the ProLibertad Freedom Campaign will 
take place on Friday, June 25, 2004, at the Martin Luther King, Jr. Labor 
Center 119/SIEU, located at 310 West 43 Street in Manhattan.  This important 
benchmark in the 10-year history of the work of ProLibertad to obtain the 
release of the Puerto Rican political prisoners and prisoners of war will be 
held from 7pm until midnight.  We are also anticipating the participation of 
friends and supporters from Puerto Rico.

The evening will be a celebration of 10 years of making freedom happen! We 
will have a minimal amount of speakers, a salsa band, spoken word, etc.  The 
food will be CRIOLLA, of course.

The 10th Anniversary Organizing Committee will be meeting in the coming days 
to nail down tickets, promotion, food, etc.

Tickets will be $25.00 for individuals, $40.00 for couples.
We will be publishing a commemorative journal and prices for ads will be as 
follows:
Full Page 8-1/2X11":  $200.00
Half Page: $100.00
1/4 Page: $50.00
Business Card Size: $25.00

Frank Velgara, ProLibertad
10th Anniversary Committee
(718) 601-4751

The evening will be a celebration of 10 years of making freedom happen! We
will have a minimal amount of speakers, a salsa band, spoken word, etc.  The
food will be CRIOLLA, of course.

The 10th Anniversary Organizing Committee will be meeting in the coming days
to nail down tickets, promotion, food, etc.

Tickets will be $25.00 for individuals, $40.00 for couples.  Please contact 
us at ProLibertad@... for tickets

Puerto Rico Delegation of the United Nations De-Colonization Committee
Hearing!!

Every year a Delegation from Puerto Rico comes to the United Nations
totestify to the U.N. De-Colonization Committee, to make the case for the
liberation of Puerto Rico and the release of the Puerto Rican
PoliticalPrisoners and Prisoners of War. This delegation is made of various
activists from the different organizations that fight for the independence
of Puerto Rico.

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign organizes a reception for this delegation
as an opportunity for allies of the Puerto Rican independence movement to
converse with the delegation about Puerto Rico in the United Nations and to
hear an update about the various struggles in Puerto Rico.

The receptions discussion topics will include:
*The workers Struggle in Puerto Rico!!
*Vieques and the Four Ds!!
*The Puerto Rican Political Prisoners!!
*Puerto Rico and the International Struggle!!
*U.S. Imperialism and Colonialism!!

Post ID:3448
Sender:"ProLibertad Campaign" <prolibertad@...>
Post Date/Time:2004-06-11 13:06:51
Subject:ProLibertad June Activities
Message:

Check out the June Updated ProLibertad Website:
http://www.ProLibertadWeb.com

******************************************************************************

Join the ProLibertad Freedom Campaign for our annual Reception for the
Puerto Rico Delegation of the United Nations De-Colonization Committee
Hearing!!

Every year a Delegation from Puerto Rico comes to the United Nations
totestify to the U.N. De-Colonization Committee, to make the case for the
liberation of Puerto Rico and the release of the Puerto Rican
PoliticalPrisoners and Prisoners of War. This delegation is made of various
activists from the different organizations that fight for the independence
of Puerto Rico.

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign organizes a reception for this delegation
as an opportunity for allies of the Puerto Rican independence movement to
converse with the delegation about Puerto Rico in the United Nations and to
hear an update about the various struggles in Puerto Rico.

The receptions discussion topics will include:
*The workers Struggle in Puerto Rico!!
*Vieques and the Four Ds!!
*The Puerto Rican Political Prisoners!!
*Puerto Rico and the International Struggle!!
*U.S. Imperialism and Colonialism!!


Monday June 14th, 2004 at 6:30pm
Hunter College West Building Second Floor Room 217
(Take the 6 train to E68th St. and Lexington Avenue)

Food, Literature, and Conversation!!

Donation: $10 (No one will be turned away)

http://www.ProLibertadWeb.com

Socialist Front
Spokesperson: Jorge Farinacci Garcia, 502-9756, 339-1692

June 14, 2004

Press Release

Shameful Melonist*Defense by the MINH at the United Nations

During the hearings that took place today by the United Nations Committee on 
Decolonizaton, 26 people testified representing the different political 
sectors in Puerto Rico.  Since 1998, the Socialist Front has participated in 
these hearings.

In our presentation we made reference to matters of great importance to our 
movement including the causes of Vieques, the political prisoners, those who 
are exiled and persecuted, the death penalty, the demilitarization of our 
universities and the denunciation by our organization of the policies of the 
Popular Democratic Party relating to the so-called status assembly of the 
people of Puerto Rico.  Today, the presenter from Pro-Commonwealth, Angel 
Ortiz, read a letter from the president of the Popular Democratic Party 
(PPD), Anibal Acevedo Vila, where he reiterates his position in favor of a 
constituent assembly with the prior approval of the United States for 2005, 
by pointing out that the relationship between this country and ours is not 
one of a colonial character.

These expressions caused dismay among the pro-independence sectors present 
and made appear ridiculous the representatives of the National Hostosiano 
Independence Movement (M.I.N.H. by its Spanish anacronim) who were there to 
defend their agreements with the Popular Democratic Party regarding this 
matter.

Yesterday, June 13th, a meeting of more than three hours took place among 
representatives from Cuba at the United Nations and sectors of the 
independence movement during which attempts were made to reach a common 
language among all those present regarding the Constituent Assembly.  The 
National Hostosiano Independence Movement (M.I.N.H.) blocked any attempt at 
consensus aluding to the limited time and how this could effect the 
resolution.  Faced with the intransigience of this organization in defense 
of the political projects of the Popular Democratic Party (PPD), Cuba opted 
not to eliminate or amend the controversial paragraph that makes reference 
to the Assembly which was imposed and only supported by the M.I.N.H.

During todays� hearings the presentations of the Socialist Front, 
Nationalist Party and other sectors of the independence movement in struggle 
drew major applause.  In contrast, the pathetic defense made in their 
presentations by the M.I.N.H. and the Puerto Rico United Nations Committee 
(COPRONU) in favor of the Assembly on Colonial Status, were received with a 
silent dramatic frigidity by those present.

The Socialist Front of Puerto Rico reiterates its denunciation of the 
shameful cabal of the Popular Democratic Party and the M.I.N.H.  We place 
responsibility squarely on this organization who promotes the politics of 
melonism for having ensared the delegation from Cuba and for the prejudicial 
consequences that this will have for the future of our struggle.  Today, for 
the first time, there was no celebration at the moment of the approval of 
the resolution.

* In Puerto Rico, red is the signature color of the colonialist Popular 
Democratic Party (PPD). Green is the signature color of the Puerto Rican 
Independence Party (PIP).  These sectors much like the Water Melon are 
pro-independence on the outside and pro-colonialist on the inside, 
independentistas supporting the colonial party, its political projects, and 
its electoral aspirations.

Support Antonio Camacho Negron!!

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign is excited to announce the release of 
Puerto Rican Political Prisoner Antonio Camacho Negron on August 13th, 
2004!!

ProLibertad would like to send Antonio a WELCOME HOME CARD with the names of 
all his supporters and some money for his transition into civilian life!!

We are asking that folks contribute to the Antonio Camacho Negron Freedom 
Fund by sending us a $25-$50-$100 donation for Antonio Camacho Negron!!  
This money will help Antonio get on his feet while he acclimates to being on 
the outside!!  Please donate generously and Support our Freedom Fighters!!

When ProLibertad sends Antonio Camacho Negron your donations, we will 
include your name in the WELCOME HOME CARD as a sponsor!!  This effort is 
open to individuals and organizations!!

If you are going to donate please make the tax-deductible donation (check or 
money order) out to IFCO/ProLibertad and WRITE IN THE MEMO SECTION FOR 
ANTONIO CAMACHO NEGRON FREEDOM FUND!!

IFCO/ProLibertad
402 W145th St
NY, NY 10031

your name to the list of Sponsors!!

all his supporters and some money for his transition into civilian life!!

We are asking that folks contribute to the Antonio Camacho Negron Freedom
Fund by sending us a $25-$50-$100 donation for Antonio Camacho Negron!!
This money will help Antonio get on his feet while he acclimates to being on
the outside!! Please donate generously and Support our Freedom Fighters!!

When ProLibertad sends Antonio Camacho Negron your donations, we will
include your name in the WELCOME HOME CARD as a sponsor!! This effort is
open to individuals and organizations!!

If you are going to donate please make the tax-deductible donation (check or
money order) out to IFCO/ProLibertad and WRITE IN THE MEMO SECTION FOR
ANTONIO CAMACHO NEGRON FREEDOM FUND!!

Send the donation to:

IFCO/ProLibertad
402 W145th St
NY, NY 10031

Then, send ProLibertad an email at ProLibertad@..., so we can add
your name to the list of Sponsors!!

OnaMOVE!
There has been an urgent development in Mumia's case which could lead to 
execution if we don't take this very seriously and unite to fight this gross 
injustice.  Recently the stay was lifted from Mumia's case which means that 
Mumia's life is in grave danger.  Below is a description of our important 
action on Sunday, July 11th along with a legal update which explains the 
situation.  Please join us on the 11th to continue to build the movement to 
save the life of Mumia Abu-Jamal.
OnaMOVE!

This year the energy that we usually spend on a July 4th demonstration will 
be used on Sunday, July 11th.  That weekend is the national conference of 
the NAACP and we will be meeting at 3pm at the Pennsylvania convention 
center at 1101 Arch St.  to hold banners, pass out leaflets, educate people 
of the grave injustice in Mumia's case and sign folks up to work.  Please 
spread the word and join us to demand freedom for Mumia Abu-Jamal, an end to 
the racist death penalty and freedom for all political prisoners.
OnaMOVE,
International Concerned Family and Friends of Mumia Abu-Jamal

July 5, 2004
On June 29, 2004, the U.S. Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit lifted its 
stay in the case of Mumia Abu-Jamal, and ordered briefing.  At issue is 
whether the death judgment should stand.  Also pending is the prosecution�s 
unconstitutional use of racism in jury selection.

Robert R. Bryan, Mumia�s lead attorney, has summed up the impact of the 
latest developments:

Mumia's case is now moving forward.  He is in extremely grave danger.  The 
authorities want to silence his voice and pen.  They thought this could be 
accomplished by convicting this innocent man and placing him on death row.  
However, his voice against injustice and oppression is now stronger then 
ever, and is heard and read throughout the world.  The government knows that 
the only way to top Mumia is to murder him in the name of the law, to 
execute him.

In over three decades of litigating death-penalty cases, I have not seen one 
in which the government wants so badly to kill a client.  We must not rest 
until Mumia is free!

The Court of Appeals briefing order came on the heels of a U.S. Supreme 
Court decision in Beard v. Banks, ___ U.S. ___, 2004 WL 1402567 (June 24, 
2004).  The issue is whether this ruling should apply to the case of Mumia.  
The prosecution is contending that the order for Mumia�s execution must 
remain and be carried out.  However, it is the view of Mr. Bryan that this 
tragically unfair decision in the Banks case should not have an effect on 
Mumia.

Mr. Bryan explained that Beard v. Banks is a complicated case.  The Supreme 
Court ruled on the appeal by Pennsylvania stemming from a Court of Appeals 
decision that invalidated the death sentence of George Banks, who has been 
on death row over 20 years for multiple murder.  Mr. Banks' death sentence 
had been overturned on the grounds that the jury instructions violated a 
Supreme Court ruling which held that jurors did not have to agree 
unanimously on the existence of mitigating circumstances in order to vote 
against death.  The issue in the Banks appeal was whether Mills v. Maryland, 
486 U.S. 367 (1988) could be applied retroactively, as the Court of Appeals 
for the Third Circuit had held.

On June 24 the Supreme Court reversed in a 5-4 decision written by Justice 
Clarence Thomas.  He concluded that the Mills case, which held 
unconstitutional capital sentencing schemes that require juries to disregard 
mitigating factors not found unanimously, did not apply retroactively.  It 
was determined that the Banks conviction became final in 1987, thus the 1988 
Mills decision did not affect his case even though what had occurred was 
unconstitutional.  Hence, Mr. Banks and others similarly situated could not 
benefit from the Mills decision and his death judgment will stand.  It is 
understood that about 30 other Pennsylvania death sentences are at stake for 
similar concerns.

Mr. Bryan pointed out that Justice Stevens, joined by Justices Souter, 
Ginsburg, and Breyer, strongly dissented.  Justice Stevens said that the use 
of such a procedure is unquestionably unconstitutional today, and I believe 
it was equally so in 1987 when respondent�s death sentence became final.  He 
further explained that Mills simply represented a straightforward 
application of our longstanding view that the Eighth and Fourteenth 
Amendments cannot tolerate the infliction of a sentence of death under [a] 
legal syste[m] that permit[s] the unique penalty to be . . . wantonly and . 
. . freakishly imposed.�  Justice Souter said that a death sentence based 
upon a verdict of 11 jurors who would have relied on a given mitigating 
circumstance to spare a defendant�s life, and a single holdout who blocked 
them from doing so, would surely be an egregious failure to express the 
public conscience accurately.  He found that too much importance is given to 
the finality of capital sentences and not enough to their accuracy.

There are other legal developments concerning the legal fight to free Mumia. 
  Robert Bryan is awaiting a ruling on a petition he filed in the trial 
court, the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia, concerning new evidence of 
innocence and prosecutorial fraud.  He will also be attempting to go back 
into the U.S. District Court regarding the statement by the trial judge, who 
said during the trial in reference to Mumia:

�Yeah, and I'm going to help'em fry the n-----.�

Robert R. Bryan, Mumia�s lead attorney, has summed up the impact of the
latest developments:

Mumia's case is now moving forward.  He is in extremely grave danger.  The
authorities want to silence his voice and pen.  They thought this could be
accomplished by convicting this innocent man and placing him on death row.
However, his voice against injustice and oppression is now stronger then
ever, and is heard and read throughout the world.  The government knows that
the only way to top Mumia is to murder him in the name of the law, to
execute him.

In over three decades of litigating death-penalty cases, I have not seen one
in which the government wants so badly to kill a client.  We must not rest
until Mumia is free!

The Court of Appeals briefing order came on the heels of a U.S. Supreme
Court decision in Beard v. Banks, ___ U.S. ___, 2004 WL 1402567 (June 24,
2004).  The issue is whether this ruling should apply to the case of Mumia.
The prosecution is contending that the order for Mumia�s execution must
remain and be carried out.  However, it is the view of Mr. Bryan that this
tragically unfair decision in the Banks case should not have an effect on
Mumia.

Mr. Bryan explained that Beard v. Banks is a complicated case.  The Supreme
Court ruled on the appeal by Pennsylvania stemming from a Court of Appeals
decision that invalidated the death sentence of George Banks, who has been
on death row over 20 years for multiple murder.  Mr. Banks' death sentence
had been overturned on the grounds that the jury instructions violated a
Supreme Court ruling which held that jurors did not have to agree
unanimously on the existence of mitigating circumstances in order to vote
against death.  The issue in the Banks appeal was whether Mills v. Maryland,
486 U.S. 367 (1988) could be applied retroactively, as the Court of Appeals
for the Third Circuit had held.

On June 24 the Supreme Court reversed in a 5-4 decision written by Justice
Clarence Thomas.  He concluded that the Mills case, which held
unconstitutional capital sentencing schemes that require juries to disregard
mitigating factors not found unanimously, did not apply retroactively.  It
was determined that the Banks conviction became final in 1987, thus the 1988
Mills decision did not affect his case even though what had occurred was
unconstitutional.  Hence, Mr. Banks and others similarly situated could not
benefit from the Mills decision and his death judgment will stand.  It is
understood that about 30 other Pennsylvania death sentences are at stake for
similar concerns.

Mr. Bryan pointed out that Justice Stevens, joined by Justices Souter,
Ginsburg, and Breyer, strongly dissented.  Justice Stevens said that the use
of such a procedure is unquestionably unconstitutional today, and I believe
it was equally so in 1987 when respondent�s death sentence became final.  He
further explained that Mills simply represented a straightforward
application of our longstanding view that the Eighth and Fourteenth
Amendments cannot tolerate the infliction of a sentence of death under [a]
legal syste[m] that permit[s] the unique penalty to be . . . wantonly and .
. . freakishly imposed.�  Justice Souter said that a death sentence based
upon a verdict of 11 jurors who would have relied on a given mitigating
circumstance to spare a defendant�s life, and a single holdout who blocked
them from doing so, would surely be an egregious failure to express the
public conscience accurately.  He found that too much importance is given to
the finality of capital sentences and not enough to their accuracy.

There are other legal developments concerning the legal fight to free Mumia.
  Robert Bryan is awaiting a ruling on a petition he filed in the trial
court, the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia, concerning new evidence of
innocence and prosecutorial fraud.  He will also be attempting to go back
into the U.S. District Court regarding the statement by the trial judge, who
said during the trial in reference to Mumia:

�Yeah, and I'm going to help'em fry the n-----.�

Post ID:3491
Sender:"ProLibertad Campaign" <prolibertad@...>
Post Date/Time:2004-08-13 15:05:31
Subject:PRican Political Prisoner Denied Release
Message:

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign
Bx 718-601-4751, Manhattan 212-927-9065, NJ 201-435-3244
ProLibertad @...
Http://www.ProLibertadweb.com

FOR IMMEDIATE RELEASE

Contact: Benjamin Ramos, 718-601-4751
ProLibertad@...


PUERTO RICAN POLITICAL PRISONER, ANTONIO CAMACHO NEGRON, HAS BEEN DENIED 
RELEASE


Friday August 13, 2004, New York, NY-  Antonio Camacho Negron, a Puerto 
Rican Political Prisoner incarcerated in FCI Allenwood, was denied release 
the morning of Friday August 13.  Camacho Negron�s family arrived at FCI 
Allenwood to receive him and were dismissed with no explanation concerning 
why his release was suspended and were denied visitation.

As of Thursday August 12, Camacho Negron�s visitation and telephone rights 
were suspended.  No reason has been given for these actions.  The 
ProLibertad Freedom Campaign is investigating the matter and will provide an 
update on Sunday August 15 at the reception and mass that has been jointly 
organized by La Iglesia San Romero De Las Americas-UCC, the church of New 
York City El Diario/La Prensa Columnist Reverend Luis Barrios.

Camacho Negron was not included in President Clinton's 1999 clemency offer, 
which 12 of the Puerto Rican Political Prisoners accepted.  He has been 
forced onto parole twice in the past five years. Each time he was paroled, 
he publicly stated that he would not recognize any parole conditions, �I 
will not legitimize the United States authority over Puerto Rico or 
myself...Puerto Rico is an illegal colony of the United States.�  Camacho 
Negron was incarcerated for violating parole conditions each time.

Camacho Negron�s upcoming release represented the culmination of his 15 year 
prison sentence and carries no parole conditions.  Yet, Camacho Negron is 
being held hostage by FCI Allenwood, unable to communicate with family or 
legal counsel.  This is a violation of his basic rights as a prisoner.

The August 15 Reception and Mass was organized as a forum for Camacho Negron 
to dialogue with community activists and leaders about the current political 
climate, the upcoming presidential election and the independence movement in 
Puerto Rico.  The Reception and Mass will proceed as planned, but will serve 
as an organizing meeting for a campaign to support Camacho Negron.


The People�s Mass and Reception is open to the media and will take place on:

Sunday August 15, 2004 at 11:30am-3pm
La Iglesia San Romero de Las Americas-UCC
2410 Amsterdam Avenue (Between w179th-180th St.) Fourth floor

-END-

Post ID:3493
Sender:"ProLibertad Campaign" <prolibertad@...>
Post Date/Time:2004-08-16 11:15:52
Subject:Update on Antonio Camacho
Message:

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign
Bx 718-601-4751, Manhattan 212-927-9065, NJ 201-435-3244
ProLibertad @..., Http://www.ProLibertadweb.com

FOR IMMEDIATE RELEASE

Contact: The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign
ProLibertad@...


PUERTO RICAN POLITICAL PRISONER, ANTONIO CAMACHO NEGRON, IS BEING HELD
INDEFINITELY


Sunday August 15, 2004, New York, NY-  Antonio Camacho Negron, a Puerto
Rican Political Prisoner incarcerated in FCI Allenwood, was denied release
the morning of Friday August 13.  According to Linda Backiel Esq., a
progressive lawyer based in Puerto Rico, a hearing to deal with the fine
that was imposed on Camacho Negron during his sentencing was never
scheduled.  Camacho Negron�s release could not occur without the hearing.
Camacho Negron, who has refused to pay the fine, denied the application for
a hearing.  Prison officials are supposed to schedule a hearing regardless
of the prisoner�s refusal to participate, but they did not.

Allegedly a hearing has been called for this upcoming week, but no official
date or time has been established.  As of now, Camacho Negron is being held
indefinitely until this hearing can take place.

Camacho Negron was not included in President Clinton's 1999 clemency offer,
which 12 of the Puerto Rican Political Prisoners accepted.  He has been
forced onto parole twice in the past five years. Each time he was paroled,
he publicly stated that he would not recognize any parole conditions, �I
will not legitimize the United States authority over Puerto Rico or
myself...Puerto Rico is an illegal colony of the United States.�  Camacho
Negron was incarcerated for violating parole conditions each time.

Camacho Negron�s upcoming release represents the culmination of his prison
sentence and carries no parole conditions.

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign is continuing to investigate this matter
and will keep our supporters, allies and the media updated as information
comes to us.

-END-

Jos� P�rez Gonz�lez, one of five Vieques Political Prisoners incarcerated in 
Puerto Rico and the United States, is being kept in inhuman conditions in a 
an Alabama jail.  Federal officials moved Perez Gonzalez to Wetumpka with no 
reason.  He is being kept in solitary conditions for 23 hours out of the 
day, without underwear and his basic hygienic needs are not being met.

As of now the ProLibertad Freedom Campaign, in conjunction with our allies

Wednesday, August 18, 2004, New York, N.Y.-Antonio Camacho Negr�n was 
released from prison on Tuesday August 17th, 2004, and now prison officials 
want him to complete two more periods of incarceration, one of 180 days and 
another of 90 days � without giving any explanation.

Camacho Negron is supposed to report to Federal Prison Guaynabo in Puerto 
Rico by Friday August 20th at 9am; he is refusing to report.  He does not

Rico.

p.m. on Delta Airlines flight 344, and will be received by a mass 
demonstration of supporters.

ANTONIO CAMACHO NEGRON RETUNRS TO PUERTO RICO SATURDAY NIGHT

Friday, August 20, 2004, New York, N.Y.-Antonio Camacho Negr�n was released 
from prison on Tuesday August 17th, 2004, and is scheduled to return to 
Puerto Rico this Saturday August 20, 2004.

Antonio was going to return to Puerto Rico Thursday night, but he was not 
issued an identification when we has released from FCI Allenwood.  This 
prevented him from departing to Puerto Rico.  As of now, that issued has 
been resolved and he will be returning to Puerto Rico on Saturday night, 
where he will be greeted by a mass support rally.

Antonio will not report to FCI Guaynabo for re-incarceration, Antonio was 
given 270 days to complete in Federal Prison Guaynabo, no reason was given 
for this extra prison time.  He will not report in on Monday morning and is 
denying this unexplained and illegal sentence addition.

-END-

Post Date/Time:2004-08-31 16:05:43
Subject:Update on Vieques PPs
Message:

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign in solidarity with our comrades in Vieques 
and in support of the freedom of the Vieques Political Prisoners, we are 
forwarding out these two new updates!!  AT THE END OF THE THIS MESSAGE YOU 
WILL ALSO FIND A NOTICE FOR A FANTASTIC REPORT BACK ORGANIZED BY THE 
VENCEREMOS BRIGADE!!


The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign
http://www.ProLibertadWeb.com
Bronx 718-601-4751
Manhattan 212-927-9065
New Jersey 201-435-3244
_______________________________________________________________________________

The Committee for the Rescue and Development of Vieques and groups in 
solidarity with the struggle for peace on Vieques, denounced the cruel and 
inhuman treatment received in US federal prisons by Jos� P�rez Gonz�lez, 
prisoner for the events of May First 2003 in Vieques. The organizations that 
participated in a conference about Vieques held in Washington, DC last May, 
include, among others: United Methodist Church; United Church of Christ, 
American Friends Service Committee (Quakers), Fellowship of Reconciliation, 
Pro Libertad in NY, National Boricua Human Rights Network, Military Toxics 
Project, All Puerto Rico with Vieques Coordinator, Menonite Church, 
Caribbean Project for Justice and Peace.

According to lawyers and family members, Jos� has been in constant movement 
from one jail to another, placed in solitary confinement on several 
occasions and transferred without knowledge of legal representatives.

In telephone conversation with the prisoner's father from Florida, he 
described how 'by the Grace of God' he found out his son had been 
transferred from an Air Force Base facility in Montgomery, Alabama to the 
Elmore County Jail in North Wetumpka, Alabama. Now, he has informed us, his 
son is in the federal prison in Atlanta, Georgia.

Representatives of human rights, environmental, cultural, religious and 
political groups in New York, New Jersey, Chicago, Massachusetts, 
California, Puerto Rico and other places, repudiate the way Federal Bureau 
of Prisons personnel carry out an obvious process of political harassment 
against Jos� P�rez. The Committee for the Rescue and Development of Vieques, 
organizations in support of the Accused and Prisoners for May First 2003 in 
Puerto Rico and the international groups will begin shortly a campaign of 
letters and calls to government officials and media to guarantee respect for 
the human rights of Jos� P�rez.  Jose Perez Gonzalez has been moved to a 
federal prison in Atlanta, Georgia.  According to Jose, His conditions have 
improved.  He is currently in general population and doing well.

Please write to Jose Perez Gonzalez and Let him know that you are thinking 
of him.

Jose Perez Gonzalez
#21519-069
Atlanta USP
PO Box 150160
Atlanta, Georgia 30315

ALSO...


Judge Fuste has imprisoned another Vieques activist, Andy Santiago!!  His 
probation officer demanded that he meet additional conditions, which he 
refused to accept.   He has been incarcerated for the remainder of his 
sentence (December 2004).

Andy Santiago #19829-069
MDC Guaynabo
P.O. Box 2147
San Juan, PR 00922-2147

Subject:Vieques Updates/Venceremos Brigade event
Message:

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign in solidarity with
our comrades in Vieques and in support of the freedom
of the Vieques Political Prisoners, we are forwarding
out these two new updates!!  AT THE END OF THE THIS
MESSAGE YOU WILL ALSO FIND A NOTICE FOR A FANTASTIC
REPORT BACK ORGANIZED BY THE VENCEREMOS BRIGADE!!


The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign
http://www.ProLibertadWeb.com
Bronx 718-601-4751
Manhattan 212-927-9065
New Jersey 201-435-3244
_______________________________________________________________________________

The Committee for the Rescue and Development of
Vieques and groups in solidarity with the struggle for
peace on Vieques, denounced the cruel and inhuman
treatment received in US federal prisons by Jos� P�rez
Gonz�lez, prisoner for the events of May First 2003 in
Vieques. The organizations that participated in a
conference about Vieques held in Washington, DC last
May, include, among others: United Methodist Church;
United Church of Christ, American Friends Service
Committee (Quakers), Fellowship of Reconciliation, Pro
Libertad in NY, National Boricua Human Rights Network,
Military Toxics Project, All Puerto Rico with Vieques
Coordinator, Menonite Church, Caribbean Project for
Justice and Peace.

According to lawyers and family members, Jos� has been
in constant movement from one jail to another, placed
in solitary confinement on several occasions and
transferred without knowledge of legal
representatives.

In telephone conversation with the prisoner's father
from Florida, he described how 'by the Grace of God'
he found out his son had been transferred from an Air
Force Base facility in Montgomery, Alabama to the
Elmore County Jail in North Wetumpka, Alabama. Now, he
has informed us, his son is in the federal prison in
Atlanta, Georgia.

Representatives of human rights, environmental,
cultural, religious and political groups in New York,
New Jersey, Chicago, Massachusetts, California, Puerto
Rico and other places, repudiate the way Federal
Bureau of Prisons personnel carry out an obvious
process of political harassment against Jos� P�rez.
The Committee for the Rescue and Development of
Vieques, organizations in support of the Accused and
Prisoners for May First 2003 in Puerto Rico and the
international groups will begin shortly a campaign of
letters and calls to government officials and media to
guarantee respect for the human rights of Jos� P�rez.
Jose Perez Gonzalez has been moved to a federal prison
in Atlanta, Georgia.  According to Jose, His
conditions have improved.  He is currently in general
population and doing well.

Please write to Jose Perez Gonzalez and Let him know
that you are thinking of him.

Jose Perez Gonzalez
#21519-069
Atlanta USP
PO Box 150160
Atlanta, Georgia 30315

ALSO...


Judge Fuste has imprisoned another Vieques activist,
Andy Santiago!!  His probation officer demanded that
he meet additional conditions, which he refused to
accept.   He has been incarcerated for the remainder
of his sentence (December 2004).

Andy Santiago #19829-069
MDC Guaynabo
P.O. Box 2147
San Juan, PR 00922-2147

Post ID:3512
Sender:"ProLibertad Campaign" <prolibertad@...>
Post Date/Time:2004-09-15 11:04:20
Subject:Sept. 17th Despierta Boricua Segment
Message:

Despierta Boricua, The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign�s fifteen-minute segment
produced for Friday wake Up Call on Puerto Rico and Puerto Rican
Politics/Culture, is airing another segment this Friday Sept. 17th, 2004 at
6:45am on WBAI 99.5fm!!

This week�s edition is on the hottest cultural/political spot to open up in
El Barrio: Camaradas El Barrio.  C A M A R A D A S el barrio
(http://camaradaselbarrio.com/) is a worker's public house where camaraderie
is built atop of a fine selection of wine, over 40 great beers from around
the world, great music and the best and boldest cuisine in Spanish Harlem.

This uniquely styled space (designed by Daniel Gonzales/ Blue Collar
Worker), reflecting an industrial and rustic feel in its wood and metal
design and decor, celebrates the spirit of factory workers and the fostering
of camaraderie in watering holes. This legacy of our working-class parents
and grandparents has become a bright star in the Spanish Harlem bar,
restaurant and entertainment scene.

Tune this Friday for Despierta Boricua WBAI 99.5fm and for those of you not
in New York you listen in via web stream at http://www.wbai.org

The ProLibertad Freedom Campaign
ProLibertad@...
http://www.ProLibertadWeb.com
Bronx 718-601-4751
Manhattan 212-927-9065
New Jersey 201-435-3244

Commemorative Activity for Richie Perez Sunday, Sept. 26th, 2004 3pm-7pm
Riverside Church 490 Riverside Drive Btw. W.120th and W.122nd St.

Invite You to Join Us to Celebrate his Extraordinary Life, Contributions and 
Legacy On Sunday, September 26th The Justice Committee/NCPRR and the Family 
of Our Brother, Comrade, Friend, and Revolutionary Richie Perez!!

Richie Perez, a former Young Lord, co-founder of the Justice Committee/ 
National Congress for Puerto Rican Rights.  Richie was a teacher, mentor, 
revolutionary and lifetime visionary who made history in the struggle for 
social justice.

On September 26th those of us who shared his life, who struggled 
side-by-side with him, those who came in contact with him in the many arenas 
of work and those who never had the opportunity to cross paths with him, but 
share a common goal and destiny should plan to join in this memorial/tribute 
to Richie.

Special performances and guest speakers include:

Alfredo de la Fe
Dave Valentin
And many more...

For more information please call 212-353-7825 or email us at 
justicecommittee@...

Readers on the CD include Marilyn herself, Sonia Sanchez, Dennis Brutus,
Genny Lim, devorah major, Carlos Quiles, Jean Stewart, Akwasi Evans, Uchechi
Kalu, Mitsuye Yamada and Chrystos. Tributes from Amiri Baraka and Kwame
Ture.

PUERTO RICAN POLITICAL PRISONERS CARLOS ALBERTO TORRES AND HAYDEE BELTRAN 
HAVE A NEW GRANDDAUGHTER!!

Maya Torres was born on Saturday September 23rd, 2004, the Grito de Lares. 
Her proud grandparents, Puerto Rican Political Prisoners Carlos Alberto 
Torres and Haydee Beltran, can�t be there to welcome her into the world. 
They can�t go to the Miami neonatal intensive care unit to support their 
daughter Clarissa, where her four pounds six ounce, one-month premature baby 
is being treated for pneumonia. They can�t help Clarissa as she recuperates 
from the Cesarian operation. They can�t baby sit Maya�s big sister, four and 
a half year old Alexandra (Munchie). They can�t just pick up the phone and 
call their daughter, even to share long distance this moment of joy in the 
family�s life. They don�t know when they�ll be able to first meet their 
granddaughter they�ll have to wait until both Clarissa and Maya are healthy 
enough to withstand the rigors of travel. While they wait, they can�t get 
emailed digital photos of this new member of their family. And speaking of 
waiting, grandma Haydee won�t be out of prison until 2010; grandpa Carlos, 
2024; both in prison since 1980.

Congratulations can be sent to grandparents

Haydee Beltran #88462-024
FCI Tallahassee
501 Capital Circle NE
Tallahassee, FL 32301

Carlos Alberto Torres
#88976-024
P.O. Box 1000
Oxford, WI 53952

and to great-grandparents Alejandrina Torres and Rev. Jose Alberto Torres, 
2724 W. Potomac, Chicago, IL 60622.

For those who wish to purchase a gift, Clarissa is registered at 
www.target.com (go to Gift Registries, and under Baby Registry type Clarissa 
Torres and Florida, then click on her name).

Larry Giddings, an anti authoritarian political prisoner was released on 
parole in August, 2004. He served more than 20 years for his 
anti-colonialist, anti-imperialist, anti-authoritarian views. The charges 
against him were adding escape, assault on police officer, conspiracy to 
effect escape and bank expropriations. He is currently staying in a half way 
house and looking for a job. To be able to continue on parole, i.e. to 
remain free he must find himself a job and place to live. Both take money.

Larry participated in the �Arts and Writings Against the Death Penalty� 
project which raised funds for Mumia Abu Jamal�s legal defense.  Political 
prisoners from around the US and from other countries would donate their 
writings, poetry, paintings, drawings, ceramics, etc to be exhibited at art 
galleries, universities, churches etc throughout the US and other countries. 
Funds raised from those that were sold were sent to Mumia�s legal defense. 
Larry contributed a number of wonderful paintings. We found out just what a 
creative and generous person he is. And now its our turn to be generous.

Please help Larry remain free and get on his feet by sending your tax 
deductible donation (check or money order made out to IFCO/Prolibertad, with 
Larry Giddings written in the memo section) to address below. Thank you

IFCO/Prolibertad
402 West 145th Street
New York, N.Y. 10031
_______________________________________________________________________________

Many of you may have known George personally; for others this may be the 
first you have heard of this IRA-gunrunning, socialist legend.

George was one of those Irish immigrants that refused to fade "from Green to 
White" as they crossed the Atlantic Ocean.  Ever the good socialist, George 
consistently took courageous stands against racism and US Imperialism.  He 
never shied away from supporting the liberation struggles of oppressed 
peoples here in the US simply because it upset the more conservative 
elements in the Irish community.  In fact, he seemed to relish in upsetting 
these elements.  I met George through the work of building an anti-racist, 
anti-imperialist pole within the Irish community in New York.  Too often 
racism went unchallenged within the community so long as someone had the 
correct "Brit's out" line relating to the north of Ireland.  George was an 
inspiration to myself and many others in challenging that attitude and 
helping to build support within the Irish community for Cuba, Mumia 
Abu-Jamal, and for Puerto Rican independence.   We have truly lost an elder 
in the fight for social justice, self-determination and socialism.  I hope 
you will take this moment to remember George as he would want to be 
remembered:  by rededicating ourselves to the struggle...George Harrison 
Presente!

George's Memorial will be held on October 20th at 6:30pm at Local 1199, 210 
W.43rd St. (between 8th  & 9th Avenues, NYC).  The speakers confirmed at 
this point are:  Bernadette Devlin McAliskey, David Dinkins, Jimmy Breslin, 
and Dennis Rivera.

Unfortunately, George never wrote his autobiography.  A friend once told me 
that when he tried to sit him down to do oral history, George would only 
talk about Mumia and Fidel--never himself. Below are a couple of articles 
about George and his illustrious career.  For more information on George's 
life and politics see The American Connection by Jack Holland, chapter 5 "Of 
Arms and the Man." (Amazon has copies for $3 bucks!)
_______________________________________________________________________________

Please see the following website to download the flyer for Farouk Abdel 
Muhti's
Memorial, taking place November 13th at 6pm, 1199.

http://sp-usa.org/newflyer.pdf
_______________________________________________________________________________

Saturday Oct. 30th, 2004 at 7pm
Hostos Community College Auditorium
149th and Grand Concourse

On October 27, 1974, over 20,000 people gathered at Madison Square Garden, 
demanding the freedom of our then political prisoners and the independence 
of Puerto Rico. With giant pictures of our nationalist heroes and our 
heroine, Lolita Lebron hanging from above, progressive and oppressed sectors 
of the North American society and over ten UN delegations.  Event was  
historical in countless other ways.

It was the first time in this country that 20,000 people came together to 
demand the freedom for our Puerto Rican Nationalist  and freedom for our 
nation.  It also proved beyond doubt the Puerto Rican community could be 
mobilized and the power of good organization  can have in mobilizing it.
However the most impressive aspect of the activity was fact that the 
majority of the people that filled the Garden  that day came from within our 
communities and from workplaces as far as Gary, Indiana where had Puerto 
Ricans had migrated to work in the steel industry.

This gathering  was the product of an intensive educational and 
organizational effort  undertaken by the members of the  Puerto Rican  
Socialist Party(PSP) �Seccional� or section of the party organized here in 
the belly of the beast in conjunction with progressive sectors in this 
country. The program included solidarity messages from representatives of 
these sectors including Dr. Angela Davis
The effort would  establish and consolidate the political and organizational 
presence of the PSP in our communities and in a number of workplaces 
resulting  in perhaps the biggest independence and socialist  Puerto Rican 
organization in this country. It continued with  a period of numerous 
struggles in many fronts from housing rent strikes to union organizing.  
Additionally   it would provide the basis and the motor for what was later 
to be the massive Bicentennial with out Colonies march held in Washington DC 
two years later in 1976.

On October 30th 2004 we will hold another gathering, this time to celebrate 
the 30th anniversary of the �Acto en el Garden� as is sometimes refered to. 
As in the 1974 activity Juan Mari Bras will be the main speaker. Juan Mari 
will be joined by representatives of some of the progressive forces in this 
country and will culminate with a cultural activity by Roy Brown.

Unfortunately not all  those who accompanied us thirty years ago will be at 
Hostos but perhaps this coming together even if you were not there the first 
time, can serve to recoup our energies, optimism and  will to continue the 
many struggles as the Garden rally did thirty years ago. Remember to join us 
on October 30th 2004, at 7:00 pm at Hostos Community College on 149th Street 
and Grand Concourse in the Bronx.
